I've uploaded a code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
s2n-tls server reports signature scheme with RSA kex
### Security issue notifications

If you discover a potential security issue in s2n we ask that you notify
AWS Security via our [vulnerability reporting page](http://aws.amazon.com/security/vulnerability-reporting/). Please do **not** create a public github issue.

### Problem:

When a TLS handshake uses RSA kex, no separate signature is required. The server proves its ownership of the RSA certificate by encrypting/decrypting the premaster secret instead.

If you negotiate with RSA kex, you will see the reasonable output from s2nc:
```
s2nc localhost 8000 --ciphers test_all_rsa_kex
libcrypto: AWS-LC 1.49.1
CONNECTED:
Handshake: NEGOTIATED|FULL_HANDSHAKE|WITH_SESSION_TICKET
Client hello version: 33
Client protocol version: 33
Server protocol version: 33
Actual protocol version: 33
Server name: localhost
Curve: NONE
Cipher negotiated: AES128-SHA
Server signature negotiated: None+None <----HERE
Early Data status: NOT REQUESTED
Wire bytes in: 2704
Wire bytes out: 498
s2n is ready
Connected to localhost:8000
```
But on the s2nd side, we do report a signature:
```
s2nd localhost 8000 --ciphers test_all_rsa_kex
libcrypto: AWS-LC 1.49.1
Listening on localhost:8000
CONNECTED:
Handshake: NEGOTIATED|FULL_HANDSHAKE|WITH_SESSION_TICKET
Client hello version: 33
Client protocol version: 33
Server protocol version: 33
Actual protocol version: 33
Server name: localhost
Curve: NONE
Cipher negotiated: AES128-SHA
Server signature negotiated: RSA+SHA256 <----HERE
Early Data status: NOT REQUESTED
JA3: a24955ad4bc89eb0c960d34b2a6f1486
Wire bytes in: 498
Wire bytes out: 2704
s2n is ready
```

I'm guessing the problem is that the server always chooses a signature scheme as part of negotiating parameters. The client doesn't know what that scheme is because the server never actually send a signature.

### Need By Date:
None, no customer reach outs. I think this is just a visibility / logging / metrics issue.

### Solution:

We should make the server also report "None+None". Likely that means updating the signature algorithm selection logic to check for RSA kex.

* **Does this change what S2N sends over the wire?** If yes, explain.
* **Does this change any public APIs?** If yes, explain.
* **Which versions of TLS will this impact?**

### Requirements / Acceptance Criteria:

What must a solution address in order to solve the problem? How do we know the solution is complete?

* **RFC links:** Links to relevant RFC(s)
* **Related Issues:** Link any relevant issues
* **Will the Usage Guide or other documentation need to be updated?**
* **Testing:** How will this change be tested? Call out new integration tests, functional tests, or particularly interesting/important unit tests.
  * **Will this change trigger SAW changes?** Changes to the state machine, the s2n_handshake_io code that controls state transitions, the DRBG, or the corking/uncorking logic could trigger SAW failures.
  * **Should this change be fuzz tested?** Will it handle untrusted input? Create a separate issue to track the fuzzing work.

### Out of scope:

Is there anything the solution will intentionally NOT address?

[//]: #  (NOTE: If you believe this might be a security issue, please email aws-security@amazon.com instead of creating a GitHub issue. For more details, see the AWS Vulnerability Reporting Guide: https://aws.amazon.com/security/vulnerability-reporting/ )


</pr_description>

    16	#include "tls/s2n_auth_selection.h"

    18	#include "crypto/s2n_certificate.h"

    20	#include "tls/s2n_cipher_suites.h"

    23	#include "utils/s2n_safety.h"

    25	/* This module should contain any logic related to choosing a valid combination of
    26	 * signature algorithm, authentication method, and certificate to use for authentication.
    27	 *
    28	 * We choose our auth methods by:
    29	 * 1. Finding a cipher suite with an auth method that we have valid certs for. In TLS1.3,
    30	 *    this is a no-op -- cipher suites do not specify an auth method.
    31	 * 2. Choosing a signature algorithm that matches both the auth method (if set) and the
    32	 *    available certs.
    33	 * 3. Selecting the cert that matches the chosen signature algorithm.
    34	 *
    35	 * This is a break from the original s2n pre-TLS1.3 flow, when we could choose certs and
    36	 * ciphers at the same time. Our cipher suites differentiate between "RSA" and "ECDSA",
    37	 * but not between "RSA" and "RSA-PSS". To make that decision, we need to wait until
    38	 * we've chosen a signature algorithm. This allows us to use RSA-PSS with existing
    39	 * TLS1.2 cipher suites.
    40	 */
    41	
    42	int s2n_get_auth_method_for_cert_type(s2n_pkey_type cert_type, s2n_authentication_method *auth_method)
    43	{
    44	    switch (cert_type) {
    45	        case S2N_PKEY_TYPE_RSA:
    46	        case S2N_PKEY_TYPE_RSA_PSS:
    47	            *auth_method = S2N_AUTHENTICATION_RSA;
    48	            return S2N_SUCCESS;
    49	        case S2N_PKEY_TYPE_ECDSA:
    50	            *auth_method = S2N_AUTHENTICATION_ECDSA;
    51	            return S2N_SUCCESS;
    52	        case S2N_PKEY_TYPE_MLDSA:
    53	        case S2N_PKEY_TYPE_UNKNOWN:
    54	        case S2N_PKEY_TYPE_SENTINEL:
    55	            POSIX_BAIL(S2N_ERR_CERT_TYPE_UNSUPPORTED);
    56	    }
    57	    POSIX_BAIL(S2N_ERR_CERT_TYPE_UNSUPPORTED);
    58	}
    59	
    60	static int s2n_is_sig_alg_valid_for_cipher_suite(s2n_signature_algorithm sig_alg, struct s2n_cipher_suite *cipher_suite)
    61	{
    62	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(cipher_suite);
    63	
    64	    s2n_pkey_type cert_type_for_sig_alg = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_UNKNOWN;
    65	    POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_signature_algorithm_get_pkey_type(sig_alg, &cert_type_for_sig_alg));
    66	
    67	    /* Non-ephemeral key exchange methods require encryption, and RSA-PSS certificates
    68	     * do not support encryption.
    69	     *
    70	     * Therefore, if a cipher suite uses a non-ephemeral kex, then any signature
    71	     * algorithm that requires RSA-PSS certificates is not valid.
    72	     */
    73	    const struct s2n_kex *kex = cipher_suite->key_exchange_alg;
    74	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(kex);
    75	    if (!kex->is_ephemeral) {
    76	        POSIX_ENSURE_NE(cert_type_for_sig_alg, S2N_PKEY_TYPE_RSA_PSS);
    77	    }
    78	
    79	    /* If a cipher suite includes an auth method, then the signature algorithm
    80	     * must match that auth method.
    81	     */
    82	    if (cipher_suite->auth_method != S2N_AUTHENTICATION_METHOD_SENTINEL) {
    83	        s2n_authentication_method auth_method_for_sig_alg;
    84	        POSIX_GUARD(s2n_get_auth_method_for_cert_type(cert_type_for_sig_alg, &auth_method_for_sig_alg));
    85	        POSIX_ENSURE_EQ(cipher_suite->auth_method, auth_method_for_sig_alg);
    86	    }
    87	
    88	    return S2N_SUCCESS;
    89	}
    90	
    91	static int s2n_certs_exist_for_sig_scheme(struct s2n_connection *conn, const struct s2n_signature_scheme *sig_scheme)
    92	{
    93	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(sig_scheme);
    94	
    95	    s2n_pkey_type cert_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_UNKNOWN;
    96	    POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_signature_algorithm_get_pkey_type(sig_scheme->sig_alg, &cert_type));
    97	
    98	    /* A valid cert must exist for the authentication method. */
    99	    struct s2n_cert_chain_and_key *cert = s2n_get_compatible_cert_chain_and_key(conn, cert_type);
   100	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(cert);
   101	
   102	    /* For TLS1.3 sig_algs that include a curve, the group must also match. */
   103	    if (sig_scheme->signature_curve && conn->actual_protocol_version >= S2N_TLS13) {
   104	        POSIX_ENSURE_REF(cert->private_key);
   105	        POSIX_ENSURE_REF(cert->cert_chain);
   106	        POSIX_ENSURE_REF(cert->cert_chain->head);
   107	        POSIX_ENSURE_EQ(cert->cert_chain->head->pkey_type, S2N_PKEY_TYPE_ECDSA);
   108	        POSIX_ENSURE_EQ(cert->cert_chain->head->info.public_key_nid, sig_scheme->signature_curve->libcrypto_nid);
   109	    }
   110	
   111	    return S2N_SUCCESS;
   112	}
   113	
   114	static int s2n_certs_exist_for_auth_method(struct s2n_connection *conn, s2n_authentication_method auth_method)
   115	{
   116	    if (auth_method == S2N_AUTHENTICATION_METHOD_SENTINEL) {
   117	        return S2N_SUCCESS;
   118	    }
   119	
   120	    s2n_authentication_method auth_method_for_cert_type;
   121	    for (int i = 0; i < S2N_CERT_TYPE_COUNT; i++) {
   122	        POSIX_GUARD(s2n_get_auth_method_for_cert_type(i, &auth_method_for_cert_type));
   123	
   124	        if (auth_method != auth_method_for_cert_type) {
   125	            continue;
   126	        }
   127	
   128	        if (s2n_get_compatible_cert_chain_and_key(conn, i) != NULL) {
   129	            return S2N_SUCCESS;
   130	        }
   131	    }
   132	    POSIX_BAIL(S2N_ERR_CERT_TYPE_UNSUPPORTED);
   133	}
   134	
   135	/* TLS1.3 ciphers are always valid, as they don't include an auth method.
   136	 *
   137	 * A pre-TLS1.3 cipher suite is valid if:
   138	 * - At least one compatible cert is configured
   139	 *
   140	 * This method is called by the server when choosing a cipher suite.
   141	 */
   142	int s2n_is_cipher_suite_valid_for_auth(struct s2n_connection *conn, struct s2n_cipher_suite *cipher_suite)
   143	{
   144	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(cipher_suite);
   145	
   146	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_certs_exist_for_auth_method(conn, cipher_suite->auth_method));
   147	
   148	    return S2N_SUCCESS;
   149	}
   150	
   151	/* A signature algorithm is valid if:
   152	 * - At least one compatible cert is configured.
   153	 * - The signature algorithm is allowed by the cipher suite's auth method
   154	 *   (if running as a pre-TLS1.3 server).
   155	 *
   156	 * This method is called by the both server and client when choosing a signature algorithm.
   157	 */
   158	int s2n_is_sig_scheme_valid_for_auth(struct s2n_connection *conn, const struct s2n_signature_scheme *sig_scheme)
   159	{
   160	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   161	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure);
   162	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(sig_scheme);
   163	
   164	    struct s2n_cipher_suite *cipher_suite = conn->secure->cipher_suite;
   165	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(cipher_suite);
   166	
   167	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_certs_exist_for_sig_scheme(conn, sig_scheme));
   168	
   169	    /* For the client side, signature algorithm does not need to match the cipher suite. */
   170	    if (conn->mode == S2N_SERVER) {
   171	        POSIX_GUARD(s2n_is_sig_alg_valid_for_cipher_suite(sig_scheme->sig_alg, cipher_suite));
   172	    }
   173	    return S2N_SUCCESS;
   174	}
   175	
   176	/* A cert is valid if:
   177	 * - The configured cipher suite's auth method (if present) supports the cert.
   178	 *
   179	 * We could also verify that at least one of our supported sig algs
   180	 * supports the cert, but that seems unnecessary. If we don't have a valid
   181	 * sig alg, we'll fail on CertVerify.
   182	 *
   183	 * This method is called by the client when receiving the server's cert.
   184	 */
   185	int s2n_is_cert_type_valid_for_auth(struct s2n_connection *conn, s2n_pkey_type cert_type)
   186	{
   187	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   188	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure);
   189	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure->cipher_suite);
   190	    s2n_authentication_method conn_auth_method = conn->secure->cipher_suite->auth_method;
   191	
   192	    /* TLS1.3 cipher suites do not specify an auth type */
   193	    if (conn_auth_method == S2N_AUTHENTICATION_METHOD_SENTINEL) {
   194	        return S2N_SUCCESS;
   195	    }
   196	
   197	    s2n_authentication_method cert_auth_method = 0;
   198	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_get_auth_method_for_cert_type(cert_type, &cert_auth_method));
   199	    POSIX_ENSURE(cert_auth_method == conn_auth_method, S2N_ERR_CERT_TYPE_UNSUPPORTED);
   200	    return S2N_SUCCESS;
   201	}
   202	
   203	/* Choose the cert associated with our configured signature algorithm.
   204	 *
   205	 * This method is called by the server after configuring its cipher suite and sig algs.
   206	 */
   207	int s2n_select_certs_for_server_auth(struct s2n_connection *conn, struct s2n_cert_chain_and_key **chosen_certs)
   208	{
   209	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   210	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme);
   211	    s2n_signature_algorithm sig_alg = conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme->sig_alg;
   212	
   213	    s2n_pkey_type cert_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_UNKNOWN;
   214	    POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_signature_algorithm_get_pkey_type(sig_alg, &cert_type));
   215	
   216	    *chosen_certs = s2n_get_compatible_cert_chain_and_key(conn, cert_type);
   217	    S2N_ERROR_IF(*chosen_certs == NULL, S2N_ERR_CERT_TYPE_UNSUPPORTED);
   218	
   219	    return S2N_SUCCESS;
   220	}

    29	static S2N_RESULT s2n_signature_scheme_validate_for_send(struct s2n_connection *conn,
    30	        const struct s2n_signature_scheme *scheme)
    31	{
    32	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
    33	
    34	    /* If no protocol has been negotiated yet, the actual_protocol_version will
    35	     * be equivalent to the client_protocol_version and represent the highest
    36	     * version supported.
    37	     */
    38	    RESULT_ENSURE_GTE(conn->actual_protocol_version, scheme->minimum_protocol_version);
    39	
    40	    /* QUIC only supports TLS1.3 */
    41	    if (s2n_connection_is_quic_enabled(conn) && scheme->maximum_protocol_version) {
    42	        RESULT_ENSURE_GTE(scheme->maximum_protocol_version, S2N_TLS13);
    43	    }
    44	
    45	    if (!s2n_is_rsa_pss_signing_supported()) {
    46	        RESULT_ENSURE_NE(scheme->sig_alg, S2N_SIGNATURE_RSA_PSS_RSAE);
    47	    }
    48	
    49	    if (!s2n_is_rsa_pss_certs_supported()) {
    50	        RESULT_ENSURE_NE(scheme->sig_alg, S2N_SIGNATURE_RSA_PSS_PSS);
    51	    }
    52	
    53	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
    54	}
    55	
    56	static bool s2n_signature_scheme_is_valid_for_send(struct s2n_connection *conn,
    57	        const struct s2n_signature_scheme *scheme)
    58	{
    59	    return s2n_result_is_ok(s2n_signature_scheme_validate_for_send(conn, scheme));
    60	}
    61	
    62	static S2N_RESULT s2n_signature_scheme_validate_for_recv(struct s2n_connection *conn,
    63	        const struct s2n_signature_scheme *scheme)
    64	{
    65	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(scheme);
    66	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
    67	
    68	    RESULT_GUARD(s2n_signature_scheme_validate_for_send(conn, scheme));
    69	
    70	    if (scheme->maximum_protocol_version != S2N_UNKNOWN_PROTOCOL_VERSION) {
    71	        RESULT_ENSURE_LTE(conn->actual_protocol_version, scheme->maximum_protocol_version);
    72	    }
    73	
    74	    RESULT_ENSURE_NE(conn->actual_protocol_version, S2N_UNKNOWN_PROTOCOL_VERSION);
    75	    if (conn->actual_protocol_version >= S2N_TLS13) {
    76	        RESULT_ENSURE_NE(scheme->hash_alg, S2N_HASH_SHA1);
    77	        RESULT_ENSURE_NE(scheme->sig_alg, S2N_SIGNATURE_RSA);
    78	    }
    79	
    80	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
    81	}
    82	
    83	static bool s2n_signature_scheme_is_valid_for_recv(struct s2n_connection *conn,
    84	        const struct s2n_signature_scheme *scheme)
    85	{
    86	    return s2n_result_is_ok(s2n_signature_scheme_validate_for_recv(conn, scheme));
    87	}
    88	
    89	static S2N_RESULT s2n_signature_algorithms_get_legacy_default(struct s2n_connection *conn,
    90	        s2n_mode signer, const struct s2n_signature_scheme **default_sig_scheme)
    91	{
    92	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
    93	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(default_sig_scheme);
    94	
    95	    s2n_authentication_method auth_method = 0;
    96	    if (signer == S2N_CLIENT) {
    97	        RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_get_auth_method_for_cert_type(
    98	                conn->handshake_params.client_cert_pkey_type, &auth_method));
    99	    } else {
   100	        RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure);
   101	        RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure->cipher_suite);
   102	        auth_method = conn->secure->cipher_suite->auth_method;
   103	    }
   104	
   105	    if (auth_method == S2N_AUTHENTICATION_ECDSA) {
   106	        *default_sig_scheme = &s2n_ecdsa_sha1;
   107	    } else {
   108	        *default_sig_scheme = &s2n_rsa_pkcs1_md5_sha1;
   109	    }
   110	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   111	}
   112	
   113	S2N_RESULT s2n_signature_algorithm_recv(struct s2n_connection *conn, struct s2n_stuffer *in)
   114	{
   115	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   116	
   117	    const struct s2n_signature_scheme **chosen_sig_scheme = NULL;
   118	    s2n_mode peer_mode = S2N_PEER_MODE(conn->mode);
   119	    if (peer_mode == S2N_CLIENT) {
   120	        chosen_sig_scheme = &conn->handshake_params.client_cert_sig_scheme;
   121	    } else {
   122	        chosen_sig_scheme = &conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme;
   123	    }
   124	
   125	    /* Before TLS1.2, signature algorithms were fixed instead of negotiated */
   126	    if (conn->actual_protocol_version < S2N_TLS12) {
   127	        return s2n_signature_algorithms_get_legacy_default(conn, peer_mode, chosen_sig_scheme);
   128	    }
   129	
   130	    uint16_t iana_value = 0;
   131	    RESULT_ENSURE(s2n_stuffer_read_uint16(in, &iana_value) == S2N_SUCCESS,
   132	            S2N_ERR_BAD_MESSAGE);
   133	
   134	    const struct s2n_signature_preferences *signature_preferences = NULL;
   135	    RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_connection_get_signature_preferences(conn, &signature_preferences));
   136	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(signature_preferences);
   137	
   138	    for (size_t i = 0; i < signature_preferences->count; i++) {
   139	        const struct s2n_signature_scheme *candidate = signature_preferences->signature_schemes[i];
   140	
   141	        if (candidate->iana_value != iana_value) {
   142	            continue;
   143	        }
   144	
   145	        if (!s2n_signature_scheme_is_valid_for_recv(conn, candidate)) {
   146	            continue;
   147	        }
   148	
   149	        *chosen_sig_scheme = candidate;
   150	        return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   151	    }
   152	
   153	    RESULT_BAIL(S2N_ERR_INVALID_SIGNATURE_SCHEME);
   154	}
   155	
   156	static S2N_RESULT s2n_signature_algorithms_validate_supported_by_peer(
   157	        struct s2n_connection *conn, uint16_t iana)
   158	{
   159	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   160	
   161	    const struct s2n_sig_scheme_list *peer_list = &conn->handshake_params.peer_sig_scheme_list;
   162	    for (size_t i = 0; i < peer_list->len; i++) {
   163	        if (peer_list->iana_list[i] == iana) {
   164	            return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   165	        }
   166	    }
   167	
   168	    RESULT_BAIL(S2N_ERR_NO_VALID_SIGNATURE_SCHEME);
   169	}
   170	
   171	static bool s2n_signature_algorithm_is_supported_by_peer(
   172	        struct s2n_connection *conn, uint16_t iana)
   173	{
   174	    return s2n_result_is_ok(s2n_signature_algorithms_validate_supported_by_peer(conn, iana));
   175	}
   176	
   177	S2N_RESULT s2n_signature_algorithm_select(struct s2n_connection *conn)
   178	{
   179	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   180	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure);
   181	    struct s2n_cipher_suite *cipher_suite = conn->secure->cipher_suite;
   182	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(cipher_suite);
   183	
   184	    const struct s2n_signature_scheme **chosen_sig_scheme = NULL;
   185	    if (conn->mode == S2N_CLIENT) {
   186	        chosen_sig_scheme = &conn->handshake_params.client_cert_sig_scheme;
   187	    } else {
   188	        chosen_sig_scheme = &conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme;
   189	    }
   190	
   191	    /* Before TLS1.2, signature algorithms were fixed instead of negotiated */
   192	    if (conn->actual_protocol_version < S2N_TLS12) {
   193	        RESULT_GUARD(s2n_signature_algorithms_get_legacy_default(conn, conn->mode, chosen_sig_scheme));
   194	        return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   195	    }
   196	
   197	    const struct s2n_signature_preferences *signature_preferences = NULL;
   198	    RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_connection_get_signature_preferences(conn, &signature_preferences));
   199	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(signature_preferences);
   200	
   201	    const struct s2n_signature_scheme *fallback_candidate = NULL;
   202	
   203	    /* We use local preference order, not peer preference order, so we iterate
   204	     * over the local preferences instead of over the options offered by the peer.
   205	     */
   206	    for (size_t i = 0; i < signature_preferences->count; i++) {
   207	        const struct s2n_signature_scheme *candidate = signature_preferences->signature_schemes[i];
   208	
   209	        /* Validates that a signature is valid to choose,
   210	         * including that it's allowed by the current protocol version.
   211	         */
   212	        if (!s2n_signature_scheme_is_valid_for_recv(conn, candidate)) {
   213	            continue;
   214	        }
   215	
   216	        if (s2n_is_sig_scheme_valid_for_auth(conn, candidate) != S2N_SUCCESS) {
   217	            continue;
   218	        }
   219	
   220	        /* s2n-tls first attempts to choose a signature algorithm offered by the peer.
   221	         * However, if that is not possible, we will attempt to continue the handshake
   222	         * anyway with an algorithm not offered by the peer. This fallback behavior
   223	         * is allowed by the RFC for TLS1.3 servers and partially allowed for TLS1.2
   224	         * servers that don't receive the signature_algorithms extension, but is
   225	         * otherwise an intentional deviation from the RFC.
   226	         *
   227	         * TLS1.3 servers:
   228	         *= https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8446#section-4.4.3
   229	         *# If the CertificateVerify message is sent by a server, the signature
   230	         *# algorithm MUST be one offered in the client's "signature_algorithms"
   231	         *# extension unless no valid certificate chain can be produced without
   232	         *# unsupported algorithms
   233	         *
   234	         * TLS1.3 clients:
   235	         *= https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8446#section-4.4.3
   236	         *= type=exception
   237	         *= reason=Compatibility with hypothetical faulty peers
   238	         *# If sent by a client, the signature algorithm used in the signature
   239	         *# MUST be one of those present in the supported_signature_algorithms
   240	         *# field of the "signature_algorithms" extension in the
   241	         *# CertificateRequest message.
   242	         *
   243	         * TLS1.2 servers:
   244	         *= https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5246#section-7.4.3
   245	         *= type=exception
   246	         *= reason=Compatibility with known faulty peers
   247	         *# If the client has offered the "signature_algorithms" extension, the
   248	         *# signature algorithm and hash algorithm MUST be a pair listed in that
   249	         *# extension.
   250	         *
   251	         * TLS1.2 clients:
   252	         *= https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5246#section-7.4.8
   253	         *= type=exception
   254	         *= reason=Compatibility with hypothetical faulty peers
   255	         *# The hash and signature algorithms used in the signature MUST be
   256	         *# one of those present in the supported_signature_algorithms field
   257	         *# of the CertificateRequest message.
   258	         */
   259	        bool is_peer_supported = s2n_signature_algorithm_is_supported_by_peer(
   260	                conn, candidate->iana_value);
   261	        if (is_peer_supported) {
   262	            *chosen_sig_scheme = candidate;
   263	            return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   264	        }
   265	
   266	        /**
   267	         *= https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5246#section-7.4.1.4.1
   268	         *# If the client does not send the signature_algorithms extension, the
   269	         *# server MUST do the following:
   270	         *#
   271	         *# -  If the negotiated key exchange algorithm is one of (RSA, DHE_RSA,
   272	         *#    DH_RSA, RSA_PSK, ECDH_RSA, ECDHE_RSA), behave as if client had
   273	         *#    sent the value {sha1,rsa}.
   274	         *#
   275	         *# -  If the negotiated key exchange algorithm is one of (DHE_DSS,
   276	         *#    DH_DSS), behave as if the client had sent the value {sha1,dsa}.
   277	         *#
   278	         *# -  If the negotiated key exchange algorithm is one of (ECDH_ECDSA,
   279	         *#    ECDHE_ECDSA), behave as if the client had sent value {sha1,ecdsa}.
   280	         *
   281	         * The default scheme for DSA is not used because s2n-tls does not support DSA certificates.
   282	         *
   283	         * These defaults are only relevant for TLS1.2, since TLS1.3 does not allow SHA1.
   284	         */
   285	        bool is_default = (candidate == &s2n_ecdsa_sha1 || candidate == &s2n_rsa_pkcs1_sha1);
   286	
   287	        /* If we ultimately cannot choose any algorithm offered by the peer,
   288	         * we will attempt negotiation with an algorithm not offered by the peer.
   289	         *
   290	         * The TLS1.2 RFC specifies default algorithms for use when no signature_algorithms
   291	         * extension is sent-- see the definition of is_default above.
   292	         *
   293	         * s2n-tls has encountered clients in the wild that support the TLS1.2
   294	         * default algorithms but do not include them in their signature_algorithms
   295	         * extension, likely due to a misreading of the RFC. So s2n-tls attempts
   296	         * to use the TLS1.2 defaults even when the client sends the signature_algorithms
   297	         * extension, and always treats them as the most preferred fallback option.
   298	         *
   299	         * If the TLS1.2 defaults are not possible-- for example, because TLS1.3
   300	         * or the security policy forbids SHA1-- we fallback to our own most
   301	         * preferred algorithm. In most cases a correctly implemented peer will reject
   302	         * this fallback, but the only alternative is to kill the connection here.
   303	         */
   304	        if (is_default) {
   305	            fallback_candidate = candidate;
   306	        } else if (fallback_candidate == NULL) {
   307	            fallback_candidate = candidate;
   308	        }
   309	    }
   310	
   311	    if (fallback_candidate) {
   312	        *chosen_sig_scheme = fallback_candidate;
   313	    } else {
   314	        RESULT_BAIL(S2N_ERR_NO_VALID_SIGNATURE_SCHEME);
   315	    }
   316	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   317	}
   318	
   319	S2N_RESULT s2n_signature_algorithms_supported_list_send(struct s2n_connection *conn, struct s2n_stuffer *out)
   320	{
   321	    const struct s2n_signature_preferences *signature_preferences = NULL;
   322	    RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_connection_get_signature_preferences(conn, &signature_preferences));
   323	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(signature_preferences);
   324	
   325	    struct s2n_stuffer_reservation size = { 0 };
   326	    RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_stuffer_reserve_uint16(out, &size));
   327	
   328	    for (size_t i = 0; i < signature_preferences->count; i++) {
   329	        const struct s2n_signature_scheme *const scheme = signature_preferences->signature_schemes[i];
   330	        RESULT_ENSURE_REF(scheme);
   331	        if (s2n_signature_scheme_is_valid_for_send(conn, scheme)) {
   332	            RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_stuffer_write_uint16(out, scheme->iana_value));
   333	        }
   334	    }
   335	    RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_stuffer_write_vector_size(&size));
   336	
   337	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   338	}
   339	
   340	int s2n_recv_supported_sig_scheme_list(struct s2n_stuffer *in, struct s2n_sig_scheme_list *sig_hash_algs)
   341	{
   342	    uint16_t length_of_all_pairs = 0;
   343	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_stuffer_read_uint16(in, &length_of_all_pairs));
   344	    if (length_of_all_pairs > s2n_stuffer_data_available(in)) {
   345	        /* Malformed length, ignore the extension */
   346	        return 0;
   347	    }
   348	
   349	    if (length_of_all_pairs % 2) {
   350	        /* Pairs occur in two byte lengths. Malformed length, ignore the extension and skip ahead */
   351	        POSIX_GUARD(s2n_stuffer_skip_read(in, length_of_all_pairs));
   352	        return 0;
   353	    }
   354	
   355	    int pairs_available = length_of_all_pairs / 2;
   356	
   357	    if (pairs_available > TLS_SIGNATURE_SCHEME_LIST_MAX_LEN) {
   358	        POSIX_BAIL(S2N_ERR_TOO_MANY_SIGNATURE_SCHEMES);
   359	    }
   360	
   361	    sig_hash_algs->len = 0;
   362	
   363	    for (size_t i = 0; i < (size_t) pairs_available; i++) {
   364	        uint16_t sig_scheme = 0;
   365	        POSIX_GUARD(s2n_stuffer_read_uint16(in, &sig_scheme));
   366	
   367	        sig_hash_algs->iana_list[sig_hash_algs->len] = sig_scheme;
   368	        sig_hash_algs->len += 1;
   369	    }
   370	
   371	    return 0;
   372	}
   373	
   374	S2N_RESULT s2n_signature_algorithm_get_pkey_type(s2n_signature_algorithm sig_alg, s2n_pkey_type *pkey_type)
   375	{
   376	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(pkey_type);
   377	    *pkey_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_UNKNOWN;
   378	
   379	    switch (sig_alg) {
   380	        case S2N_SIGNATURE_RSA:
   381	        case S2N_SIGNATURE_RSA_PSS_RSAE:
   382	            *pkey_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_RSA;
   383	            break;
   384	        case S2N_SIGNATURE_RSA_PSS_PSS:
   385	            *pkey_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_RSA_PSS;
   386	            break;
   387	        case S2N_SIGNATURE_ECDSA:
   388	            *pkey_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_ECDSA;
   389	            break;
   390	        case S2N_SIGNATURE_MLDSA:
   391	            *pkey_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_MLDSA;
   392	            break;
   393	        default:
   394	            RESULT_BAIL(S2N_ERR_INVALID_SIGNATURE_ALGORITHM);
   395	    }
   396	
   397	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   398	}

    32	static int s2n_server_key_send_write_signature(struct s2n_connection *conn, struct s2n_blob *signature);
    33	
    34	int s2n_server_key_recv(struct s2n_connection *conn)
    35	{
    36	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn);
    37	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure);
    38	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure->cipher_suite);
    39	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure->cipher_suite->key_exchange_alg);
    40	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->handshake.hashes);
    41	
    42	    struct s2n_hash_state *signature_hash = &conn->handshake.hashes->hash_workspace;
    43	    const struct s2n_kex *key_exchange = conn->secure->cipher_suite->key_exchange_alg;
    44	    struct s2n_stuffer *in = &conn->handshake.io;
    45	    struct s2n_blob data_to_verify = { 0 };
    46	
    47	    /* Read the KEX data */
    48	    struct s2n_kex_raw_server_data kex_data = { 0 };
    49	    POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_kex_server_key_recv_read_data(key_exchange, conn, &data_to_verify, &kex_data));
    50	
    51	    POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_signature_algorithm_recv(conn, in));
    52	    const struct s2n_signature_scheme *active_sig_scheme = conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme;
    53	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(active_sig_scheme);
    54	
    55	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_hash_init(signature_hash, active_sig_scheme->hash_alg));
    56	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_hash_update(signature_hash, conn->handshake_params.client_random, S2N_TLS_RANDOM_DATA_LEN));
    57	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_hash_update(signature_hash, conn->handshake_params.server_random, S2N_TLS_RANDOM_DATA_LEN));
    58	
    59	    /* Add KEX specific data */
    60	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_hash_update(signature_hash, data_to_verify.data, data_to_verify.size));
    61	
    62	    /* Verify the signature */
    63	    uint16_t signature_length = 0;
    64	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_stuffer_read_uint16(in, &signature_length));
    65	
    66	    struct s2n_blob signature = { 0 };
    67	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_blob_init(&signature, s2n_stuffer_raw_read(in, signature_length), signature_length));
    68	
    69	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(signature.data);
    70	    POSIX_ENSURE_GT(signature_length, 0);
    71	
    72	    S2N_ERROR_IF(s2n_pkey_verify(&conn->handshake_params.server_public_key, active_sig_scheme->sig_alg, signature_hash, &signature) < 0,
    73	            S2N_ERR_BAD_MESSAGE);
    74	
    75	    /* We don't need the key any more, so free it */
    76	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_pkey_free(&conn->handshake_params.server_public_key));
    77	
    78	    /* Parse the KEX data into whatever form needed and save it to the connection object */
    79	    POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_kex_server_key_recv_parse_data(key_exchange, conn, &kex_data));
    80	    return 0;
    81	}
    82	
    83	int s2n_ecdhe_server_key_recv_read_data(struct s2n_connection *conn, struct s2n_blob *data_to_verify,
    84	        struct s2n_kex_raw_server_data *raw_server_data)
    85	{
    86	    struct s2n_stuffer *in = &conn->handshake.io;
    87	
    88	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_ecc_evp_read_params(in, data_to_verify, &raw_server_data->ecdhe_data));
    89	    return 0;
    90	}

s2nd is an s2n-tls server testing utility.
It is not intended for production use.

usage: s2nd [options] host port
 host: hostname or IP address to listen on
 port: port to listen on

 Options:

  -a [protocol]
  --alpn [protocol]
    Sets a single application protocol supported by this server.
  -c [version_string]
  --ciphers [version_string]
    Set the cipher preference version string. Defaults to "default" 
  --enter-fips-mode
    Enter libcrypto's FIPS mode. The linked version of OpenSSL must be built with the FIPS module.
  --cert
    Path to a PEM encoded certificate [chain]. Option can be repeated to load multiple certs.
  --key
    Path to a PEM encoded private key that matches cert. Option can be repeated to load multiple certs.
  -m
  --mutualAuth
    Request a Client Certificate. Any RSA Certificate will be accepted.
  -n
  --negotiate
    Only perform tls handshake and then shutdown the connection
  --parallelize
    Create a new Connection handler thread for each new connection. Useful for tests with lots of connections.
    Warning: this option isn't compatible with TLS Resumption, since each thread gets its own Session cache.
  --prefer-low-latency
    Prefer low latency by clamping maximum outgoing record size at 1500.
  --prefer-throughput
    Prefer throughput by raising maximum outgoing record size to 16k
  --enable-mfl
    Accept client's TLS maximum fragment length extension request
  --ocsp
    Path to a DER formatted OCSP response for stapling
  -s
  --self-service-blinding
    Don't introduce 10-30 second delays on TLS Handshake errors. 
    Warning: this should only be used for testing since skipping blinding may allow timing side channels.
  -t,--ca-file [file path]
    Location of trust store CA file (PEM format). If neither -t or -d are specified. System defaults will be used.    This option is only used if mutual auth is enabled.
  -d,--ca-dir [directory path]
    Directory containing hashed trusted certs. If neither -t or -d are specified. System defaults will be used.    This option is only used if mutual auth is enabled.
  -i,--insecure
    Turns off certification validation altogether.
  --stk-file
    Location of key file used for encryption and decryption of session ticket.
  -T,--no-session-ticket
    Disable session ticket for resumption.
  -C,--corked-io
    Turn on corked io
  --non-blocking
    Set the non-blocking flag on the connection's socket.
  -w --https-server
    Run s2nd in a simple https server mode.
  -b --https-bench <bytes>
    Send number of bytes in https server mode to test throughput.
  -L --key-log <path>
    Enable NSS key logging into the provided path
  -P --psk <psk-identity,psk-secret,psk-hmac-alg> 
    A comma-separated list of psk parameters in this order: psk_identity, psk_secret and psk_hmac_alg.
    Note that the maximum number of permitted psks is 10, the psk-secret is hex-encoded, and whitespace is not allowed before or after the commas.
    Ex: --psk psk_id,psk_secret,SHA256 --psk shared_id,shared_secret,SHA384.
  -E, --max-early-data 
    Sets maximum early data allowed in session tickets. 
  -N --npn 
    Indicates support for the NPN extension. The '--alpn' option MUST be used with this option to signal the protocols supported.  -h,--help
    Display this message and quit.
  --buffered-send <buffer size>
    Set s2n_send to buffer up to <buffer size> bytes before sending records over the wire.
  -X, --max-conns <max connections>
    Sets the max number of connections s2nd will accept before shutting down.

2026-05-29 00:51:59,027 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT


🎬 ACTION
cat > /tmp/repro_rsa_kex_sig.sh <<'EOF'
#!/usr/bin/env bash
set -euo pipefail
PORT=${PORT:-45678}
S2ND=/testbed/build/bin/s2nd
S2NC=/testbed/build/bin/s2nc
CERT=/testbed/tests/pems/rsa_2048_sha256_wildcard_cert.pem
KEY=/testbed/tests/pems/rsa_2048_pkcs8_key.pem
SERVER_OUT=$(mktemp)
CLIENT_OUT=$(mktemp)
cleanup() {
  if [[ -n "${SERVER_PID:-}" ]]; then kill "$SERVER_PID" 2>/dev/null || true; wait "$SERVER_PID" 2>/dev/null || true; fi
  rm -f "$SERVER_OUT" "$CLIENT_OUT"
}
trap cleanup EXIT
"$S2ND" --cert "$CERT" --key "$KEY" --ciphers test_all_rsa_kex --negotiate --max-conns 1 127.0.0.1 "$PORT" >"$SERVER_OUT" 2>&1 &
SERVER_PID=$!
for i in $(seq 1 50); do
  if grep -q "Listening" "$SERVER_OUT"; then break; fi
  sleep 0.1
done
"$S2NC" --ciphers test_all_rsa_kex -i 127.0.0.1 "$PORT" >"$CLIENT_OUT" 2>&1 || { cat "$SERVER_OUT"; cat "$CLIENT_OUT"; exit 1; }
wait "$SERVER_PID" || true
SERVER_SIG=$(grep "Server signature negotiated" "$SERVER_OUT" | tail -1 || true)
CLIENT_SIG=$(grep "Server signature negotiated" "$CLIENT_OUT" | tail -1 || true)
echo "server: ${SERVER_SIG}"
echo "client: ${CLIENT_SIG}"
if echo "$SERVER_SIG" | grep -q "None+None"; then
  echo "FIXED"
  exit 0
else
  echo "BUG"
  exit 2
fi
EOF
chmod +x /tmp/repro_rsa_kex_sig.sh

   742	
   743	        printf("Connected to %s:%s\n", host, port);
   744	
   745	        /* Save session state from connection if reconnect is enabled. */
   746	        if (reconnect > 0 || ticket_out) {
   747	            if (conn->actual_protocol_version >= S2N_TLS13) {
   748	                if (!session_ticket) {
   749	                    print_s2n_error("s2nc can only reconnect in TLS1.3 with session tickets.");
   750	                    exit(1);
   751	                }
   752	                GUARD_EXIT(echo(conn, sockfd, &session_ticket_recv), "Error calling echo");
   753	            } else {
   754	                if (!session_ticket && s2n_connection_get_session_id_length(conn) <= 0) {
   755	                    print_s2n_error("Endpoint sent empty session id so cannot resume session");
   756	                    exit(1);
   757	                }
   758	                free(session_state);
   759	                session_state_length = s2n_connection_get_session_length(conn);
   760	                session_state = calloc(session_state_length, sizeof(uint8_t));
   761	                GUARD_EXIT_NULL(session_state);
   762	                if (s2n_connection_get_session(conn, session_state, session_state_length) != session_state_length) {
   763	                    print_s2n_error("Error getting serialized session state");
   764	                    exit(1);
   765	                }
   766	            }
   767	            if (ticket_out) {
   768	                GUARD_EXIT(write_array_to_file(ticket_out, session_state, session_state_length), "Failed to write to ticket-out file");
   769	            }
   770	        }
   771	
   772	        if (dyn_rec_threshold > 0 && dyn_rec_timeout > 0) {
   773	            s2n_connection_set_dynamic_record_threshold(conn, dyn_rec_threshold, dyn_rec_timeout);
   774	        }
   775	
   776	        GUARD_EXIT(s2n_connection_free_handshake(conn), "Error freeing handshake memory after negotiation");
   777	
   778	        if (send_file != NULL) {
   779	            printf("Sending file contents:\n%s\n", send_file);
   780	
   781	            unsigned long send_file_len = strlen(send_file);
   782	            s2n_blocked_status blocked = S2N_NOT_BLOCKED;
   783	            send_data(conn, sockfd, send_file, send_file_len, &blocked);
   784	        }
   785	
   786	        while (echo_input) {
   787	            fflush(stdout);
   788	            fflush(stderr);
   789	            echo(conn, sockfd, &reneg_ctx.do_renegotiate);
   790	
   791	            if (!reneg_ctx.do_renegotiate) {
   792	                break;
   793	            }
   794	
   795	            reneg_ctx.do_renegotiate = false;
   796	            GUARD_EXIT(renegotiate(conn, sockfd), "Renegotiation failed");
   797	        }
   798	
   799	        if (serialize_out) {
   800	            GUARD_EXIT(s2n_connection_serialize_out(conn, serialize_out), "Error serializing connection");
   801	        } else {
   802	            GUARD_EXIT(wait_for_shutdown(conn, sockfd), "Error closing connection");
   803	        }
   804	
   805	        GUARD_EXIT(s2n_connection_free(conn), "Error freeing connection");
   806	
   807	        GUARD_EXIT(s2n_config_free(config), "Error freeing configuration");
   808	
   809	        close(sockfd);
   810	        reconnect--;

#!/usr/bin/env bash
set -euo pipefail
PORT=${PORT:-8000}
S2ND=/testbed/build/bin/s2nd
S2NC=/testbed/build/bin/s2nc
CERT=/testbed/tests/pems/rsa_2048_sha256_wildcard_cert.pem
KEY=/testbed/tests/pems/rsa_2048_pkcs8_key.pem
SERVER_OUT=$(mktemp)
CLIENT_OUT=$(mktemp)
cleanup() {
  if [[ -n "${SERVER_PID:-}" ]]; then kill "$SERVER_PID" 2>/dev/null || true; wait "$SERVER_PID" 2>/dev/null || true; fi
  rm -f "$SERVER_OUT" "$CLIENT_OUT"
}
trap cleanup EXIT
"$S2ND" --cert "$CERT" --key "$KEY" --ciphers test_all_rsa_kex --negotiate --max-conns 1 127.0.0.1 "$PORT" >"$SERVER_OUT" 2>&1 &
SERVER_PID=$!
for i in $(seq 1 100); do
  if grep -q "Listening" "$SERVER_OUT"; then break; fi
  sleep 0.05
done
timeout 5 "$S2NC" --ciphers test_all_rsa_kex -i --send-file /dev/null 127.0.0.1 "$PORT" >"$CLIENT_OUT" 2>&1 || { cat "$SERVER_OUT"; cat "$CLIENT_OUT"; exit 1; }
wait "$SERVER_PID" || true
SERVER_SIG=$(grep "Server signature negotiated" "$SERVER_OUT" | tail -1 || true)
CLIENT_SIG=$(grep "Server signature negotiated" "$CLIENT_OUT" | tail -1 || true)
echo "server: ${SERVER_SIG}"
echo "client: ${CLIENT_SIG}"
if echo "$SERVER_SIG" | grep -q "None+None"; then
  echo "FIXED"
  exit 0
else
  echo "BUG"
  exit 2
fi
EOF

cat > /tmp/repro_rsa_kex_sig.sh <<'EOF'
#!/usr/bin/env bash
set -euo pipefail
PORT=${PORT:-8000}
S2ND=/testbed/build/bin/s2nd
S2NC=/testbed/build/bin/s2nc
CERT=/testbed/tests/pems/rsa_2048_sha256_wildcard_cert.pem
KEY=/testbed/tests/pems/rsa_2048_pkcs8_key.pem
SERVER_OUT=$(mktemp)
CLIENT_OUT=$(mktemp)
cleanup() {
  if [[ -n "${SERVER_PID:-}" ]]; then kill "$SERVER_PID" 2>/dev/null || true; wait "$SERVER_PID" 2>/dev/null || true; fi
  rm -f "$SERVER_OUT" "$CLIENT_OUT"
}
trap cleanup EXIT
"$S2ND" --cert "$CERT" --key "$KEY" --ciphers test_all_rsa_kex --negotiate -X 1 127.0.0.1 "$PORT" >"$SERVER_OUT" 2>&1 &
SERVER_PID=$!
for i in $(seq 1 100); do
  if grep -q "Listening" "$SERVER_OUT"; then break; fi
  sleep 0.05
done
timeout 5 "$S2NC" --ciphers test_all_rsa_kex -i --send-file /dev/null 127.0.0.1 "$PORT" >"$CLIENT_OUT" 2>&1 || { cat "$SERVER_OUT"; cat "$CLIENT_OUT"; exit 1; }
wait "$SERVER_PID" || true
SERVER_SIG=$(grep "Server signature negotiated" "$SERVER_OUT" | tail -1 || true)
CLIENT_SIG=$(grep "Server signature negotiated" "$CLIENT_OUT" | tail -1 || true)
echo "server: ${SERVER_SIG}"
echo "client: ${CLIENT_SIG}"
if echo "$SERVER_SIG" | grep -q "None+None"; then
  echo "FIXED"
  exit 0
else
  echo "BUG"
  exit 2
fi
EOF
chmod +x /tmp/repro_rsa_kex_sig.sh
/tmp/repro_rsa_kex_sig.sh; exit 0

   148	static int s2n_set_cert_chain_as_client(struct s2n_connection *conn)
   149	{
   150	    if (s2n_config_get_num_default_certs(conn->config) > 0) {
   151	        struct s2n_cert_chain_and_key *cert = NULL;
   152	        if (conn->config->cert_request_cb) {
   153	            struct s2n_certificate_request request = { 0 };
   154	            /* Don't try to free this stuffer, it's purely for reading pre-existing blob that outlives it. */
   155	            POSIX_GUARD(s2n_stuffer_init_written(&request.list.iterator, &conn->cert_authorities));
   156	            POSIX_ENSURE(conn->config->cert_request_cb(conn, conn->config->cert_request_cb_ctx, &request) == S2N_SUCCESS, S2N_ERR_CANCELLED);
   157	            cert = request.chain;
   158	            POSIX_ENSURE(cert, S2N_ERR_NO_CERT_FOUND);
   159	        } else {
   160	            cert = s2n_config_get_single_default_cert(conn->config);
   161	            POSIX_ENSURE_REF(cert);
   162	        }
   163	        conn->handshake_params.our_chain_and_key = cert;
   164	        conn->handshake_params.client_cert_pkey_type = s2n_cert_chain_and_key_get_pkey_type(cert);
   165	
   166	        POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_signature_algorithm_select(conn));
   167	    }
   168	
   169	    return 0;
   170	}

    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure);
    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure->cipher_suite);
    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure->cipher_suite->key_exchange_alg);
    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme);

    s2n_pkey_type cert_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_UNKNOWN;
    if (s2n_kex_includes(conn->secure->cipher_suite->key_exchange_alg, &s2n_rsa)) {
        /* RSA key exchange uses an RSA encryption certificate, but does not use
         * a separate server signature scheme.

        cert_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_RSA;

        POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_signature_algorithm_get_pkey_type(sig_alg, &cert_type));

    S2N_ERROR_IF(*chosen_certs == NULL, S2N_ERR_CERT_TYPE_UNSUPPORTED);

    return S2N_SUCCESS;

 /* Choose the cert associated with our configured signature algorithm.
+ * For RSA key exchange, no signature algorithm is used, so choose an RSA cert.
  *
  * This method is called by the server after configuring its cipher suite and sig algs.
  */
 int s2n_select_certs_for_server_auth(struct s2n_connection *conn, struct s2n_cert_chain_and_key **chosen_certs)
 {
     POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn);
+    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure);
+    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure->cipher_suite);
+    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure->cipher_suite->key_exchange_alg);
     POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme);
-    s2n_signature_algorithm sig_alg = conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme->sig_alg;
 
     s2n_pkey_type cert_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_UNKNOWN;
-    POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_signature_algorithm_get_pkey_type(sig_alg, &cert_type));
+    if (s2n_kex_includes(conn->secure->cipher_suite->key_exchange_alg, &s2n_rsa)) {
+        /* RSA key exchange uses an RSA encryption certificate, but does not use
+         * a separate server signature scheme.
+         */
+        cert_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_RSA;
+    } else {
+        s2n_signature_algorithm sig_alg = conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme->sig_alg;
+        POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_signature_algorithm_get_pkey_type(sig_alg, &cert_type));
+    }
 
     *chosen_certs = s2n_get_compatible_cert_chain_and_key(conn, cert_type);
     S2N_ERROR_IF(*chosen_certs == NULL, S2N_ERR_CERT_TYPE_UNSUPPORTED);

+    /* RSA key exchange does not use a server signature. The server proves
+     * possession of the RSA private key by decrypting the premaster secret.
+     */
+    if (conn->mode == S2N_SERVER && s2n_kex_includes(cipher_suite->key_exchange_alg, &s2n_rsa)) {
+        *chosen_sig_scheme = &s2n_null_sig_scheme;
+        return S2N_RESULT_OK;
+    }
+
     /* Before TLS1.2, signature algorithms were fixed instead of negotiated */
     if (conn->actual_protocol_version < S2N_TLS12) {
         RESULT_GUARD(s2n_signature_algorithms_get_legacy_default(conn, conn->mode, chosen_sig_scheme));
